     574           1 : //       able to call them. Closure can also do so. To avoid that, add your function to
     575           1 : //       the exports using something like

     704           1 : // allocate(): This is for internal use. You can use it yourself as well, but the interface
     705           1 : //             is a little tricky (see docs right below). The reason is that it is optimized
     706           1 : //             for multiple syntaxes to save space in generated code. So you should
     707           1 : //             normally not use allocate(), and instead allocate memory using _malloc(),
     708           1 : //             initialize it with setValue(), and so forth.

     711           1 : //        affect this!)

     713           1 : //         or a single type which is used for the entire block. This only matters if there
     714           1 : //         is initial data - if @slab is a number, then this does not matter at all and is
     715           1 : //         ignored.

    1275           2 : function reSign(value, bits, ignore) {
    1276           2 :   if (value <= 0) {
    1277           2 :     return value;
    1278           2 :   }

    1280           2 :                         : Math.pow(2, bits-1);

    1283           2 :                                                        // TODO: In i64 mode 1, resign the two parts separately and safely
    1284           2 :     value = -2*half + value; // Cannot bitshift half, as it may be at the limit of the bits JS uses in bitshifts
